  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1d4120f3-eb4f-46b6-ac5b-b9bc0d10bd5a'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer14789915383382377802">Wisdom to Create a Life of Passion, Purpose, and Peace<br/><br/>This inspiring tale provides a step-by-step approach to living with greater courage, balance, abundance, and joy. A wonderfully crafted fable, <em>The Monk Who Sold His Ferrari</em> tells the extraordinary story of Julian Mantle, a lawyer forced to confront the spiritual crisis of his out-of-balance life. On a life-changing odys</span>
  <span id="freeText14789915383382377802" style="display:none">Wisdom to Create a Life of Passion, Purpose, and Peace<br /><br />This inspiring tale provides a step-by-step approach to living with greater courage, balance, abundance, and joy. A wonderfully crafted fable, <em>The Monk Who Sold His Ferrari</em> tells the extraordinary story of Julian Mantle, a lawyer forced to confront the spiritual crisis of his out-of-balance life. On a life-changing odyssey to an ancient culture, he discovers powerful, wise, and practical lessons that teach us to:<br /><br /><br />Develop Joyful Thoughts, Follow Our Life's Mission and Calling, Cultivate Self-Discipline and Act Courageously, Value Time as Our Most Important Commodity, Nourish Our Relationships, and Live Fully, One Day at a Time.</span>

      </div>

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/55006114-gaurang"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1460891395i/55006114._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/55006114-gaurang">Gaurang</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Motivation for what? To read it? <br/>It does not "seem" like ..but it is indeed a self help book. May be looks drama to you because you are already helped<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Motivation for what? To read it? <br />It does not "seem" like ..but it is indeed a self help book. May be looks drama to you because you are already helped..hahaha. <br />I always thought the audience of the book was american people, where the moto is more or less..."we can do everything". The thirst for big cars and million dollar businesses. But I recently had a friend get motivated enough by this book to keep herself busy during the confinement. I read this way back and kind of became a bit more productive. Learned to organise my time for better things. <br />I still think one can fall in the trap of being too productive. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14786812127536824241">Loved the message, just didn't like the format it was presented in. Felt like the author just had a list of frequently asked questions and set out to answer each and every one of them one by one systematically, so there wasn't much narrative or actual enjoyment in the reading of it. The "story" is essentially just 2 guys talking over dinner, actually only 1 guy talking (the titular Monk), the other guy is just there to ask the questions in between the long monologues and to confirm the Monk's an</span>
  <span id="freeText14786812127536824241" style="display:none">Loved the message, just didn't like the format it was presented in. Felt like the author just had a list of frequently asked questions and set out to answer each and every one of them one by one systematically, so there wasn't much narrative or actual enjoyment in the reading of it. The "story" is essentially just 2 guys talking over dinner, actually only 1 guy talking (the titular Monk), the other guy is just there to ask the questions in between the long monologues and to confirm the Monk's answers. I felt the listener of the story was pretty naive, he seemed to just take everything his monk friend said without question, and we're led to believe that through one night of lecturing he is enlightened; perhaps his mystical friend hypnotised him!!! GASP! However, despite all my criticism with the characters and the non-existent story, I am glad that the subject matter was written simply without using convoluted and deep spiritual words; it could have so easily have gone that way.</span>

<div id="review_515087622" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/515087622" />
    <a title="jenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/998805-jenna"><img alt="jenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1205879303p2/998805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/515087622?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jenna" href="/user/show/998805-jenna">jenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/998805-jenna?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/998805-jenna?shelf=spoofs">spoofs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/998805-jenna?shelf=raspberry-sound-here">raspberry-sound-here</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer515087622" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9750232319003490130">I categorized this book under spoofs because it made me laugh so much. I wanted to stop reading it because I found it ridiculous, but I wouldn't feel worthy of panning it here if I hadn't completed it and the joy of sharing my take on this book kept me turning pages and dog-earring quotable pages.<br/><br/>First, let me be clear, I like me some cheese; I like it with crackers and I like it with wine and I like it in my entertainment and personal growth. That this book is cheesier than a Velveeta factory w</span>
  <span id="freeText9750232319003490130" style="display:none">I categorized this book under spoofs because it made me laugh so much. I wanted to stop reading it because I found it ridiculous, but I wouldn't feel worthy of panning it here if I hadn't completed it and the joy of sharing my take on this book kept me turning pages and dog-earring quotable pages.<br /><br />First, let me be clear, I like me some cheese; I like it with crackers and I like it with wine and I like it in my entertainment and personal growth. That this book is cheesier than a Velveeta factory was not the problem. The problem is that you have to back cheese up with some realism to make it relatable and digestable. Sharma does not do this.<br /><br />Sharma did one thing that I very much did like, at least he may have done this, naming the book. It's a great title and made me want to read it immediately as I already had the book outlined in my head based upon the title and it was very good. I should have stuck with my own fantasy. Instead, there's a ton of new age advice espoused thru a very dumb fable that serves as some new age pnuemonic (which it takes John, the "student", most of the book to get and then is praised heavily by Julian, "the teacher" for this observation like a special ed teacher giving a student a lollipop for looking both ways before crossing the street. Actually, this typifies most of their interactions... only a special ed student would eventually become resentful of the condescension... But this never happens to John because he is a complete idiot, oh, sorry, I mean "empty cup". He's more like an empty thimble who's practically ejaculating over every trite concept Julian throws his way with wide eyed awe.). <br /><br />Maybe these immaculate revelations would have had more of an impact on me as a teenager, but you would've had to get to me in early adolescence to impress me with the wonder of "think positive thoughts!", "prioritize what's important in your life!", "live in the now!", "find a purpose!", etc. etc. I love new age ideas and concepts, but Sharma just reguritates other people's wisdom and doesn't even make it interesting or unique. He even quotes himself from the book in the book! Each lesson has a summary of key ideas, actions, etc. and in each one he quotes himself, from the chapter you JUST READ, which has to earn him Douche of the Month, if not DOTYear in my opinion. <br /><br />He is also an awful writer, most evident in his use of speaker tags and abuse of adjectives, which were actually my favorite part of the book-they were that bad. here are some fun examples:<br /><br />"'Do I have to find a special lake to apply the Secret of the Lake?' I asked innocently."<br /><br />"Hardly 'new age,'" he said, with a broad grin lighting up his radiant face.<br /><br />Julian remembering the monks:<br />"I still remember seeing these wonderful looking people seated on the little bamboo chairs reading their strangely bound books with the subtle smiles of enlightenment unforlding across their lips."<br /><br />"Easy, big fella! I couldn't agree with you more," offered Julian with all the warth and patience of a wise, loving grandfather.<br /><br />Here's my favorite part of the book. John is talking about his big belly:<br />"It's really not that big," Julian suggested in a consoling tone.<br />"Then why does Jenny call me Mr. Donut?" I said, breaking into a broad smile.<br />Julian started to laugh. I had to follow. Soon the two of us were howling on the floor.<br />"I guess if you can't laugh at yourself who can you laugh at?" I said, still giggling.<br /><br />Oh, I could go on and on, because Sherma does in this same manner. Sigh, it feels good to get this out. In summary, the book doesn't espouse anything bad or incorrect, it just does it in a really pathetic and sometimes insultingly condescending way.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9750232319003490130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1474131511" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1474131511" />
    <a title="Adina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22189348-adina"><img alt="Adina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531917330p2/22189348.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1474131511?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adina" href="/user/show/22189348-adina">Adina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22189348-adina?shelf=india">india</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22189348-adina?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22189348-adina?shelf=short">short</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1474131511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10661140710603832405">I am not a fan of personal development books written by so called motivational writers. I prefer writers that have previously done something with their life. However, I received this as a gift from my best friend and I was feeling a little bit under the weather so I felt that some motivation was welcomed. I tried to keep my heart open and was prepared to absorb as many life-changing advices as possible. <br/><br/>I knew the book was total garbage from the first 20 pages but I tried to give it a chance and</span>
  <span id="freeText10661140710603832405" style="display:none">I am not a fan of personal development books written by so called motivational writers. I prefer writers that have previously done something with their life. However, I received this as a gift from my best friend and I was feeling a little bit under the weather so I felt that some motivation was welcomed. I tried to keep my heart open and was prepared to absorb as many life-changing advices as possible. <br /><br />I knew the book was total garbage from the first 20 pages but I tried to give it a chance and pressed on. I read so many reviews that claimed that reading this changed their life so I thought that it must be me. After I realized that it is not me but the book I still kept reading so I can write an informed hate review. So there it is. <br /><br />The Monk who sold his Ferrari makes me think about a fish stew, and not a good one. Usually, in fish stews you add different kinds of leftover fish and seafood that is not very fresh but not gone bad either. Then, you put a lot of tomato juice and condiments to give a strong taste so nobody knows that the fish is not at their best. This book feels the same. The author collected a variety of cliche, already discussed ideas such as positive thinking, meditation, goal prioritization, focus, getting up early, more exercise and yes, oh yes, eating of live food aka becoming a vegetarian. The last bit almost made me to throw the book to a wall. So, what do you do when you have absolutely nothing new to say but you want to make it interesting so everybody buys your book? Bingo, you use a fable. Everybody loves one, right? So, in order to touch the main target group, the depressed corporate employee, you take a lawyer as a main character. You add a bit of drama, a heart attack, which pushes the hero to quit his job and leave in a quest to find himself? Where does the hero go? You guessed it…India, of course. After he spends some time with a very isolated yogi group in the Himalayas he comes back to the US enlightened, looking 30 years younger and ready to help others find the true path to happiness and health. The first victim is a colleague lawyer to whom our hero presents the complex ancient philosophy in one night. Yup, this is all it takes to become a new person. Most of the book is a dialogue between the “monk” and his moronic friend. The disciple is so entranced by the sage of his mentor that he agrees with everything he says, no questions are asked and all the proposed techniques and ideas are immediately adopted. I sometime wondered if hypnotization was used. <br /><br />Maybe I could have digested all these ideas if the book had been well written. Which it wasn’t. A 10 year old could have done a better job. It was boring and ridiculous. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10661140710603832405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3389247234" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3389247234" />
    <a title="Krystal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18989854-krystal"><img alt="Krystal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491478087p2/18989854.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3389247234?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krystal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krystal" href="/user/show/18989854-krystal">Krystal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/23002737-the-monk-who-sold-his-ferrari">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=sep-2020">sep-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=recs-and-reputation">recs-and-reputation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=disappointments">disappointments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=think-deep">think-deep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=hippie-stuff">hippie-stuff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3389247234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9474583639330604459">Once again I am disappointed by a book because I misunderstood what I was getting into.<br/><br/>I honestly thought this was a biographical account of a dude who really did sell all his posessions and wander off to discover the meaning of life. But that's just the ruse the author uses to tell you what <i>he</i> believes are the secrets of life.<br/><br/><b>It's basically a beginner's insight into spiritual development</b> in a form similar to both <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35239798.The_Courage_to_be_Disliked' title='The Courage to be Disliked by Ichiro Kishimi' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Courage to be Disliked</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18144590.The_Alchemist' title='The Alchemist by Paulo Coelho' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Alchemist</a>, in that <b>it uses a fictional discussi</b></span>
  <span id="freeText9474583639330604459" style="display:none">Once again I am disappointed by a book because I misunderstood what I was getting into.<br /><br />I honestly thought this was a biographical account of a dude who really did sell all his posessions and wander off to discover the meaning of life. But that's just the ruse the author uses to tell you what <i>he</i> believes are the secrets of life.<br /><br /><b>It's basically a beginner's insight into spiritual development</b> in a form similar to both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35239798.The_Courage_to_be_Disliked" title="The Courage to be Disliked by Ichiro Kishimi" rel="nofollow noopener">The Courage to be Disliked</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18144590.The_Alchemist" title="The Alchemist by Paulo Coelho" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alchemist</a>, in that <b>it uses a fictional discussion between two characters to deliver all its wisdom.</b><br /><br />Unfortunately, there wasn't anything new enough here to make up for my disappointment at being jipped on the motivational biography I thought this was.<br /><br /><u>The setup is this:</u> Julian is a hotshot lawyer who has a heart attack one day in court. This serves as his wakeup call so he sells everything he owns then goes off to India to live among sages who will teach him the meaning of life. Then he comes back and passes on all this wisdom to his hotshot lawyer protege, and this book is essentially that conversation between the two.<br /><br />Firstly, <b>it's a bit of a stretch</b> that this protege is so open to changing every single aspect of his life so dramatically, and the sporadic attempts at humour just make this more ridiculous. The setup is a poor one, because it's so unrealistic, which doesn't exactly inspire confidence in the methods. It all ends up feeling rather far-fetched instead of practical - and this from a person who completely supports the seven points that are made.<br /><br /><b>It's almost like the author was too lazy to provide actual facts, figures and examples,</b> so just put all is own thoughts into these two fictional creations. I guess the point is to make it more accessible but it made it seem phony and conceited to me. I guess the delivery just really rubbed me the wrong way.<br /><br />But aside from that, <b>the concepts it provides <i>are</i> actually quite useful,</b> and it's all stuff I've read repeatedly in books on personal development. It just simplifies it all, which is what I mean about being 'Spirituality for Beginners'. I'm not denying the information, but it just barely scratches the surface. Ironically, it's like the 'quick-fix' version of personal development.<br /><br />So overall I hated the delivery and it was a little too basic for me, but I do support the information it conveys and think this is a great entry point for anyone who may be looking to begin a little self development.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9474583639330604459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11710020127841339773">The monk who sold his Ferrari, is a misleading title. The man who sold his Ferrari and became a monk, would have been more accurate. The idea of a monk driving a Ferrari is somewhat thought provoking and made me smile. The book itself was a merger between fiction and instruction on techniques to perfect your life experience. From a fiction point of view, it too often told rather than showed. It’s an easy to read book (I read it in an afternoon) and the structure works well making it easy to reme</span>
  <span id="freeText11710020127841339773" style="display:none">The monk who sold his Ferrari, is a misleading title. The man who sold his Ferrari and became a monk, would have been more accurate. The idea of a monk driving a Ferrari is somewhat thought provoking and made me smile. The book itself was a merger between fiction and instruction on techniques to perfect your life experience. From a fiction point of view, it too often told rather than showed. It’s an easy to read book (I read it in an afternoon) and the structure works well making it easy to remember what went before, or where to look for a particular part.<br />However, I don’t feel helped. I don’t feel like my life has been enlightened. I feel like I’ve been told to get up earlier in the morning and meditate. I could have told me that before. Somehow, I couldn’t believe in these monks doing their one handed press-ups at 4am every morning. I felt sorry for them. What sort of enlightenment requires being in the same village forever? How did the monks know about the real world if they didn’t experience it? <br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_805974419" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/805974419" />
    <a title="Catherine Howard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3500204-catherine-howard"><img alt="Catherine Howard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446100547p2/3500204.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/805974419?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catherine Howard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catherine Howard" href="/user/show/3500204-catherine-howard">Catherine Howard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19060872-the-monk-who-sold-his-ferrari">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer805974419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8790596705416395459">Outing myself as a reader of self-improvement books with this review, but so what... I think it's all a bit of a waste of time if you don't try to spend some of your time improving your life from within. <br/><br/>THE MONK WHO SOLD HIS FERRARI didn't start off well for me because I absolutely detest fables; my idea of cruel and unusual punishment is being forced to re-read THE CELESTINE PROPHECY, for example. My problem with fables is that they are, more often than not, stupid. They come across as a child</span>
  <span id="freeText8790596705416395459" style="display:none">Outing myself as a reader of self-improvement books with this review, but so what... I think it's all a bit of a waste of time if you don't try to spend some of your time improving your life from within. <br /><br />THE MONK WHO SOLD HIS FERRARI didn't start off well for me because I absolutely detest fables; my idea of cruel and unusual punishment is being forced to re-read THE CELESTINE PROPHECY, for example. My problem with fables is that they are, more often than not, stupid. They come across as a childish and often condescending way to get a point across when straight forward non-fiction would've done the job. They also tend to be written by people who, while extremely wise and with something very worthwhile and interesting to say, have no flair for writing fiction, and the whole thing just ends up being clunky, cheesy and unreadable, a faint burn of embarrassment for the author coming to your cheeks as you read. <br /><br />I've just described the first 2-3 chapters of this book, but please: push through. I'm so glad I did. There's so many great insights in this book, and endless quotations for you to highlight or stick somewhere prominent. Of course, a lot of it is common sense, but what do you expect? The answer to the meaning of life? (Although Sharma actually has an answer for that: the meaning of life is to live a life of meaning.) And it introduced me to a Carl Jung quotation that's now one of my favourites: "he who looks outside dreams, he who looks inside awakens."<br /><br />Great reading on the eve of a New Year and definitely worth a re-read with a highlighter. Just grit your teeth and push through those first few chapters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8790596705416395459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7467137982351904389">The Monk Who Sold His Ferrari is basically a self help book told in the format of a story. It is filled with positivity and motivation. And there is plenty of wisdom in the book. <br/><br/>But the book does seem ridiculous at times and it feels like one is reading an infomercial script. <br/><br/>The book did uplift me and filled me with positive vibes at times, but it still didn't convince me to sell my Ferrari (if I had one).</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8666606569659182724"><b>Genre</b>: Spiritual<br/><b>Publication Date</b>: 1996<br/><br/>This is one of the better books in the realm of personal development in close association with spirituality. <br/><br/>The story is of Julian Mantle, a hotshot lawyer who has everything that money can buy, who has his life turned around when he gets a heart attack in the midst of a courtroom. He then goes to the mysterious land of India to get away from the fast paced frenzy and to rediscover his soul and find his true purpose and meaning in life.<br/><br/>Here he is met with s</span>
  <span id="freeText8666606569659182724" style="display:none"><b>Genre</b>: Spiritual<br /><b>Publication Date</b>: 1996<br /><br />This is one of the better books in the realm of personal development in close association with spirituality. <br /><br />The story is of Julian Mantle, a hotshot lawyer who has everything that money can buy, who has his life turned around when he gets a heart attack in the midst of a courtroom. He then goes to the mysterious land of India to get away from the fast paced frenzy and to rediscover his soul and find his true purpose and meaning in life.<br /><br />Here he is met with sages of sivana, the monks who live in the cold mountain regions, living a complete life in terms of mind, body and soul, being happy and living till the age of 100 and above. Julian learns a lot about how to live life in search of true meaning. He learns about the virtues that can enable him to be more full and happier.<br /><br />The writing is straight forward, the progression of events very peaceful, and the journey described very thought provoking and at times enlightening.</span>

<div id="review_96542496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96542496" />
    <a title="Muthazhagu Palanisamy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3410909-muthazhagu-palanisamy"><img alt="Muthazhagu Palanisamy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1268123153p2/3410909.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96542496?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Muthazhagu Palanisamy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Muthazhagu Palanisamy" href="/user/show/3410909-muthazhagu-palanisamy">Muthazhagu Palanisamy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96542496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11439984071414616407">A lot irritated by the narration, but not the content.<br/><br/>May be it is my prejudice - I find the "fable" approach to self-help books tedious to read. The last one I read, that took a similar approach, was Gung Ho! by Ken Blanchard, and came off thinking that the whole book was silly. The Monk Who... came highly recommended, and hence I plunged in.<br/><br/>The book starts off on a promising note - hot-shot lawyer has a heart-attack in court, right after winning a big case. What happens next? <br/><br/>Here's what happe</span>
  <span id="freeText11439984071414616407" style="display:none">A lot irritated by the narration, but not the content.<br /><br />May be it is my prejudice - I find the "fable" approach to self-help books tedious to read. The last one I read, that took a similar approach, was Gung Ho! by Ken Blanchard, and came off thinking that the whole book was silly. The Monk Who... came highly recommended, and hence I plunged in.<br /><br />The book starts off on a promising note - hot-shot lawyer has a heart-attack in court, right after winning a big case. What happens next? <br /><br />Here's what happens - India - Himalayas - Yogi - "a lot of finding myself" - Mystical land - Mystical procedures (apparently even the Pareto technique!) - "share these with others" - another bad fable, within this already bad fable. You can fill in the blanks with that info. <br /><br />And oh, throw in really really really (big emphasis on that third really) bad jokes as part of the "conversation".<br /><br />Grrrrroooooaaann :(.<br /><br />Not to sound overly negative, there were things that hit home for me. <br /><br />Summarizing them below - <br />1. Take care of yourself first. If you can't do even that, how can you take care of others / work?<br />2. Maintain strict discipline in training your body, and your mind.<br />3. Setting aside some "quiet time" on a daily basis.<br />4. Goal setting - committing to a goal publicly, so that you hold yourselves accountable in front of your peers.<br />5. Reflect on what you did good / bad the previous day, and make points for improvement on a daily basis.<br />6. Get your priorities right - not a lot of people on their death-bed wishing that they had spent more time at work.<br /><br />This book could have been a LOT BETTER had the author dropped the "fable approach", and just presented his ideas in a straight-forward manner. I like Robin Sharma's The Greatness Guide (Book 2) better than this one, for this reason.<br /><br />Skip it, if you can resist the folks giving over-the-top reviews for this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11439984071414616407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/507947169" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/507947169?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abhilash Kulkarni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abhilash Kulkarni" href="/user/show/16492499-abhilash-kulkarni">Abhilash Kulkarni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16492499-abhilash-kulkarni?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer507947169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9595838188297018221">Some books are meant to be tasted, some are meant to chewed, some digested. While there are some rare books that not only meant to be digested but also made to be a part of the body and mind. The Monk Who Sold His Ferrari is one such book. <br/>The books moves at a good pace and the never becomes boring as peachy books tend to be. In fact, the way the teachings have been presented in a story format is the most important reason why this book has become so popular among the masses. It also lasts only 2</span>
  <span id="freeText9595838188297018221" style="display:none">Some books are meant to be tasted, some are meant to chewed, some digested. While there are some rare books that not only meant to be digested but also made to be a part of the body and mind. The Monk Who Sold His Ferrari is one such book. <br />The books moves at a good pace and the never becomes boring as peachy books tend to be. In fact, the way the teachings have been presented in a story format is the most important reason why this book has become so popular among the masses. It also lasts only 200-odd pages hence can easily be completed on a long train or road journey. It took me three days to complete the book as I had other things to do, but at my normal pace I could have easily competed it in 4-5 hours. However this is not a book which is meant to be read quickly and forgotten, and is best read slowly. It takes some time to understand some of the teachings, and requires inflection as to how they can be applied in our own life. The teachings are simple and some of them are well-known. But the presentation of the ideas is what sets this book apart from other books.<br />All of the teachings can be remembered by the simple story of the sumo wrestler told in the book.<br />On a personal level, and this book has certainly caused a lot of change in my life. I am feeling in myself a new energy, something which I had lost for a few years.<br />Read thoroughly and applied diligently, this book has the potential to transform our lives. Although its not practically possible to apply each and everyone of the teachings (As I later found out), this book fully deserves the accolades it has been getting, and should be made a part of our system. I wouldn't have even started writing all these reviews if it hadn't been for this book, and as I usually only think about doing things but never actually do it. This book compelled me to live the life that I have always dreamed about. It has also made me see positive things in life<br />. It has taught me to be clear about what you want from life and direct your entire focus towards it, and not get affected by the trivialities that surround it. I am extremely grateful to Robin Sharma for penning such a wonderful book</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_491567840" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/491567840" />
    <a title="Ru" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3959348-ru"><img alt="Ru" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1309018858p2/3959348.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/491567840?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ru" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ru" href="/user/show/3959348-ru">Ru</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062515" href="/book/show/8853467-the-monk-who-sold-his-ferrari">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer491567840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12027993157686918643">This book feels like a patronizing practical joke. But the agony you feel reading it is very real. This is the printed equivalent of when the Hare Krishna community would stop you on the street or at the airport and tell you all about the Bhagavad Gita, and no matter how politely you declined to hear more, they wouldn't let you leave. This is not a long book by any means, but you'd never know it. Let me get to my problems with it, which seem numerous, but at the same time I don't even want to in</span>
  <span id="freeText12027993157686918643" style="display:none">This book feels like a patronizing practical joke. But the agony you feel reading it is very real. This is the printed equivalent of when the Hare Krishna community would stop you on the street or at the airport and tell you all about the Bhagavad Gita, and no matter how politely you declined to hear more, they wouldn't let you leave. This is not a long book by any means, but you'd never know it. Let me get to my problems with it, which seem numerous, but at the same time I don't even want to invest the time in writing a lengthy review of it, since it has robbed me of enough life essence already.<br /><br />I mistakenly thought this would be a humorous, poignant read, involving the dichotomy of a monk and a Ferrari. That sounds like a fun book to read, and I wanted to start 2013 off on a joyful note. At no point does a monk sell a Ferrari in these pages; it's simply something that has occurred in the so-called monk's life. The monk is more of a man who is essentially "reborn" spiritually in India and passes along what he has learned to his former colleague and friend. That would be fine, but these teachings are incredibly dogmatic and come across as judgmental and preachy. Basically, every single lesson is to "stop doing every single thing you currently do, do the opposite, so long as it's what I do, repeat it X times a day/week, and you will live longer and better!" It's like snake oil in scripted form. Had this story simply been more suggestive than demanding, it would have been much better served.<br /><br />The other perhaps more glaring problem is that this is a horribly-written story. It comes off like a bad Grade 8 essay, except that one can forgive a bad Grade 8 essay's author, because he's only in Grade 8. Robin Sharma doesn't have an excuse nearly close to that in any way, shape, or form. Every single scene seems so incredibly contrived and pandering, which leaves it being soulless and emotionless, which is ironic, because it's almost certainly trying for the exact opposite effect. Sharma should one day reveal a small child did indeed write this book for him for a few coppers, and I might give him an ounce of respect.<br /><br />I could go on and on about the faults of some of the specifics of this fable, but I am sleepy. Let me say this: if you are at the end of your rope, and by that I mean suicidal, and looking for hope in the form of a book, then perhaps this is the book for you, but I would also suggest any number of "try this!" books would help. That's the only reason I rate this two stars over one, frankly. Make your own life choices, stand by them, and if they happen to coincide with the contents of this silly story, then great, and if they don't, then also great (or perhaps even greater).</span>
  <a data-text-id="12027993157686918643" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/121111423?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bianda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bianda" href="/user/show/407130-bianda">Bianda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062515" href="/book/show/8853467-the-monk-who-sold-his-ferrari">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121111423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18018296844820339992">A spiritual journey of a hot-shot lawyer who owns a 'fabolous' life and a ferrari, and eventually turns himself to become a monk and live a truly enlightened life.<br/>He shares his amazing experience and new wisdom that he has gained to his former colleague. These wisdoms are shared throughout the entire book.<br/>Most of them are really inspirational to live a life full of purpose.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_44740111" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/44740111" />
    <a title="Samer Hijazi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1937225-samer-hijazi"><img alt="Samer Hijazi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515058371p2/1937225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/44740111?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samer Hijazi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samer Hijazi" href="/user/show/1937225-samer-hijazi">Samer Hijazi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer44740111" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15734586726628499532">Read this book if you want to add a new dimension to your life. It is the first spiritual book I read. Usually I didn’t go for such books for the reason that seeking more into religion would cover it. Now I realize that regardless of your religion, these books contain vital knowledge and information that you might encounter for the first time in your life. One topic which was innovative and influential is the inner spiritual serenity, self-knowledge and self-control. I always had a glimpse of it</span>
  <span id="freeText15734586726628499532" style="display:none">Read this book if you want to add a new dimension to your life. It is the first spiritual book I read. Usually I didn’t go for such books for the reason that seeking more into religion would cover it. Now I realize that regardless of your religion, these books contain vital knowledge and information that you might encounter for the first time in your life. One topic which was innovative and influential is the inner spiritual serenity, self-knowledge and self-control. I always had a glimpse of it but never thought it was indulged in such books.<br /><br />No matter what life or what personality are you, no matter what a state are you in, this book will open up a new dimension to regularly use in our lives, a new dimension that fits all your worries, troubles, ambitions, dreams and most important your inner being. You’ll value life more when you read this book and find wonders in yourself. No need to add it to your reading list, just grab it and start reading. No matter how much you read, when and where, it’s all good for your inside and outside. These words of wisdom are clustered in a matter of 200 pages. Give it a try and join me in this new dimension. <br /><br />Sharma is indeed interesting on how he presents spiritual teachings in a novel form. At some points it seems repetitive and maybe so simple, but everything is placed in a good sequence and it is well paced. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15734586726628499532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15429590652955540852">2019<br/>A timely reminder that you can change your life at anytime. <br/><br/>January 14, 2018<br/>"The Monk Who Sold My Ferrari" is one of my favorite books to (re)read at the start of the year.   <span id="freeText15429590652955540852" style="display:none">2019<br />A timely reminder that you can change your life at anytime. <br /><br />January 14, 2018<br />"The Monk Who Sold My Ferrari" is one of my favorite books to (re)read at the start of the year. This book never disappoints and it was great getting a reminder of all the things I need to focus on to make this a great year. Too often we get all caught up in the rat race and as this book succinctly puts it, "even if you win the rat race you are still a rat".<br />I do try daily to incorporate the 10 Rituals of Radiant Living, it really helps putting these daily rituals at the focal point of your life, it will really improve your year. <br />Must. Read.<br /><br /><br />This book is life changing. It changed my life. CHANGED. <br />Everyone should read it and keep re-reading it. <br /><br />Read this book for the first time in August 2014. I decided to re-read it for the start of the new year and I was not disappointed. This is a life changing book, providing you follow the instructions given by the Monk. The book outlines simple practical steps on how to change your life and keep it changed. <br />Go read it!</span>

<div id="review_2446029772" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2446029772" />
    <a title="Neelam Babul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9945293-neelam-babul"><img alt="Neelam Babul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588932157p2/9945293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2446029772?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neelam Babul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neelam Babul" href="/user/show/9945293-neelam-babul">Neelam Babul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788179921623" href="/book/show/43882.The_Monk_Who_Sold_His_Ferrari">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2446029772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16371167282781829437">I first read this book back in high school when a friend recommended it to me. At that time I did enjoy reading the book but not being a huge fan of self help books I just out it aside occasionally reading the summaries on the book or quotes related to the book to inspire and motivate myself. Since then I have widened my reading forte including self help, personal development, biography, memoirs and many others in order to not just view reading as a way of relaxing but also as a way of growing a</span>
  <span id="freeText16371167282781829437" style="display:none">I first read this book back in high school when a friend recommended it to me. At that time I did enjoy reading the book but not being a huge fan of self help books I just out it aside occasionally reading the summaries on the book or quotes related to the book to inspire and motivate myself. Since then I have widened my reading forte including self help, personal development, biography, memoirs and many others in order to not just view reading as a way of relaxing but also as a way of growing and continuously learning and improving my life. <br /><br />I re-read this book today and I must say I realized what a great mistake I had done. If only I had understood the book at that age and worked on its principles I would be in a far better place than I am today. <br /><br />The writer conveys his insights in the form of a fable where a lawyer turned monk guides his protegee to adapt a life which will help him lead a prosperous, uplifting, fulfilling and virtuous life. Using short stories as a medium, the writer casts a way for us to understand and adopt the seven principles which will help us lead purposeful lives. These principles include:<br /><br />1. Master your mind;<br />2. Follow your purpose;<br />3. Practice Kaizen;<br />4. Live with discipline;<br />5. Respect your time;<br />6. Selflessly serve others; and<br />7. Embrace the present. <br /><br />This is a book you need to read multiple times to nurture your mind, body and soul at every point in one's life. <br /><br />A marvelous, splendid and superb book that is a timeless classic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16371167282781829437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RNQ4vLTd8hOgGgtSwMRk6OU6fUXQ+4yYLKpVr9GbyNZo2g5dpEdq8lALnhTXySlRn7+p6ilQWo69wgqPHXU8Iw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  <span id="freeText10095329159908952771" style="display:none">Robin Sharma is one of the world’s premier thinkers on leadership, personal growth and life management. The bestselling author of <br />The Monk Who Sold His Ferrari, <br />Who Will Cry When You Die? and <br />The Saint, the Surfer, and the CEO and four other books on self-transformation. <p>Robin Sharma is in constant demand internationally as keynote speaker at the conferences of many of the most powerful companies on the planet including Microsoft, Nortel Networks, General Motors, FedEx and IBM. He is a resident of Ontario, Canada. (Barnes and Noble)<br /></p></span>
